# **83 - What Sleeps In The Heart Of Stillness (3)**

“W-what are you doing!?”

“Bern!?”

Marī screamed, and Alex’s eyes widened in shock.

Alex instinctively reached for the hilt of his sword but couldn’t point the tip at him.

My mind and body were also unable to keep up with the sudden turn of events.

“To think a place like this existed beneath Marra… No wonder it wasn’t found even after 100 years. This is the very definition of a blind spot.”

Bernkatze leisurely stepped forward, muttering to himself. Contrary to his calm tone, he walked as if he were trampling the floor. It was clear that he harbored a strong murderous aura in his heart. A black haze leaked from the gaps in his armor, from his entire body. An evil presence. He clearly radiated the aura of something non-human.

“You’re not the real Bernkatze! Show your true self!!”

“Heheheh! If you’ve figured it out, I guess I have no choice!”

Saying that, Bernkatze roughly cast off his helmet.

The filthy sludge stuck inside the helmet scattered around as he did so.

The mud-covered furnishings sizzled and emitted black smoke.

A stale stench spread in an instant.

It felt like a pure white cloth was being defiled with tar.

The clean air quickly rotted away.

What appeared from under the helmet was a man with a shallowly carved face. At a glance, he looked to be over 25. It was unclear whether his hair and eyes were naturally black or if they were dyed by the color of the black Mara that covered half of his face. However, his eyes, twisted into an ugly sneer with hostility and malice, seemed to be the exact opposite of his original temperament. It was too distorted.

He wore a circlet with a red gemstone embedded in his forehead. It was a teardrop-shaped gem. The stone, as if it had a consciousness of its own, occasionally emitted a sharp, rainbow glow. The gem on Bernkatze’s forehead and the giant crystal enshrined in the center of the room radiated the exact same color of light.

“That circlet on your forehead! The glow of that gem—it’s the Cintāmaṇi accessory!”

“Correct. You are quite knowledgeable, as expected.”

We all gathered near Alex, who had a grim expression.

Bernkatze’s behavior was no ordinary matter.

Everyone took a combat stance in preparation for anything.

“That gem is a powerful Magic Tool that seals a person’s thoughts and consciousness. Bernkatze’s body has been taken over and is being controlled by some malevolent will that resides in that circlet.”

“What!? Can’t we do something about it?”

“Maybe with a Marra legacy.”

“So we need to search inside this palace?”

“…Cindy, Zarumen. Can I ask this of the two of you?”

I couldn’t nod immediately at the instructions Alex gave.

Alex, with his pale face, seemed to be in a tough spot both physically and mentally. It felt wrong to leave him here like this. A worst-case scenario flashed through my mind like lightning.

Marī and Clair sinking in a pool of blood. Bernkatze too. The only one left standing in this place was Alex with the ominously glowing circlet. Such an ominous image welled up within me.

But how could I convince him?

“Leave it to Cindy.”

Saying that, she strongly pulled my hand, which was hesitating.

“Zaryū, you’re strong now. You can protect everyone.”

“…Understood, Zarumen, please stay with us. Cindy, look for the treasury. There must be something there.”

“Okay!”

I saw Cindy off as she bolted out of the room like a fleeing rabbit.

“What, only one person ran away? I was waiting for you since this body is the young master’s childhood friend… It’s not too late to run, young master, is it?”

“Hah! Spreading oily killing intent and then acting so innocent! It’s infuriating to see you impersonate Bernkatze with that body!”

The air sizzled.

His anger took on magic power and turned into flames.

Alex was so enraged that magic power was leaking out of him naturally.

“…Ah, it’s a pain that the body’s habits and gestures immediately take over if I’m not careful. And the original owner of this body keeps whining and making a racket in my ear… It’s a convenient cheat item for infinite continues, but the usability is bad in that regard.”

In contrast, Bernkatze nonchalantly brushed it off.

No, not brushing it off, but not even listening.

He was muttering to himself as if he had no interest.

Infinite Continues.

Cheat Item.

No matter how I looked at it, the words that came out were not from this world.

Combined with the sense of incongruity I had earlier, there was no doubt now.

His true identity was a Reincarnator. And.

“Well, it doesn’t matter, I guess. The best thing is that there’s no limit on the number of uses. This body isn’t that strong, and I don’t really like the face… but the biggest advantage is that I can easily switch to a body I like.”

Only his eyes moved, glaring at Alex.

“A high-level Adventurer with a handsome face and a harem—he’s perfect for my next body! The women are high-level, too, and I bet I can have fun with them, too!”

A chill ran through my entire body. His cold, appraising gaze.

He didn’t see us as humans.

“Some useless trash guy is attached to them, but I can just kill him and use him for experience points.”

I was the same as a broken toy to be thrown away.

It was the same look I had received so many times at the Guild.

I gritted my teeth in frustration.

Even if my Level increased, my heart didn’t become strong.

Even if I pretended not to notice, the trauma ingrained in me tangled my feet.

“My comrade—”

A red light flashed like lightning.

“Don’t insult Zarumen!”

Alex charged forward, an arrow of crimson trailing behind him.

“—You bastard!!”

A strike cloaked in flames that spread like wings.

The intense heat scorched the surrounding walls and ceiling.

Alex’s anger had exploded.

The magic power drawn out by his intense emotions was burning fiercely.

“Gah, is he part of your harem, too? For a handsome guy, you have bad taste in men, young master.”

Bernkatze continued to spew insults.

His mantle was burnt away, but he didn’t seem to have taken any further damage.

The sword that received the full force of the blow was covered in that black sludge.

“I don’t have that kind of relationship with him!”

“Oh, really… Then you’re waiting to be attacked?”

“I’ll kill you! I’ll definitely kill you!”

“Hahahaha! Hey, weren’t you supposed to get this body back for its owner!? You’re just agitated because I hit a sore spot!”

“…That’s not it! Haaah!!”

The sword covered in black mud swelled significantly, forming a malevolent blade.

Bernkatze handled the greatsword, which was unbefitting a knight, with ease. Alex’s swordsmanship, delivered with a roar and a whirlwind of wind and fire. Bernkatze seemed to have enough room to spare to just laugh and parry it. In fact, the amount of darkness overflowing from Bernkatze’s body was gradually increasing.

Every time the darkness increased, the black greatsword grew even bigger.

The increased darkness moved sluggishly, deflecting Alex’s strike like a shield. I didn’t know the logic behind it, but it was clear that the longer this went on, the more disadvantaged we would become.

“Hah, hah, hah… Damn it!”

“Whoops, young master, are you out of breath already? You can’t satisfy anyone like that!”

“Shut up!”

“Alex!”

An invited strike. He slipped into my open guard.

The sludge-covered left arm of the man reached out to grab Alex’s face.

“Burst!”

Marī’s magic exploded at the last moment. As a dry sound of bursting air echoed, Bernkatze’s body was lifted slightly into the air. The invisible bullets hit only the enemy’s body without missing their mark.

It was a difficult feat to intervene in a warrior’s close-quarters combat without hitting a stray shot.

And it was a strike meant to avert a fatal moment, one that had to be delivered at that precise second.

How many people could perform the same feat?

“Oh, this is amazing. You’re traveling with a capable woman. It might be good to switch to her instead.”

“You must be ki—”

“—dding me! I would never give my Marī to a scumbag like you!”

I roared, cutting into Alex’s words.

My emotions had impulsively jumped out of my mouth.

“…Whose am I?”

Marī’s ears were a little red as she muttered in an exasperated tone.

“Oh, my… It seems you were heartbroken, young master?”

This was probably because I was not in his line of sight.

Bernkatze’s face looked as if he had been shot by a popgun.

“…Hmph, what a foolish man. I’ve told you many times that Zarumen and I don’t have that kind of frivolous relationship…”

Alex, who had been sweating profusely, slowly regulated his breathing.

“Come back, Bernkatze. How long are you going to be a puppet for such a pathetic man?”

“Guh, Gaah… Young… master, I’m so… sorry…!”

For a moment, the light returned to Bernkatze’s eyes. But soon, the black haze covered his eyes again. It hardened just like the sword, becoming a black armor that dominated Bernkatze’s body.

“Damn it! Why does a small fry have to resist so much!? It’s annoying! You guys just need to shut up and offer me your asses, and that’s all!!”

Bernkatze revealed his frustration at his lack of progress.

The greatsword he swung wildly caused destruction all around, but Alex, who had become calm in contrast, was now parrying it instead. The offense and defense had switched. I couldn’t just leave his rampage unchecked.

“Woooooooh! All of you, just die!!”

A shadowy arm grew out of Bernkatze’s back.

It swung wildly, and a projectile the size of a fist was released.

It was aimed at us. He was likely enraged by our meddling.

The bullet, forged from killing intent and curses, seemed to contain fatal power.

But all of those attacks were blocked by an invisible wall.

Everything shattered in midair. He glared at us with a look of hatred.

His eyes then fell on Clair, who was kneeling on the floor, praying deeply.

“A priestess’s Barrier! You damn insolent pest…!”

Magic that borrowed power from praying to Gods. That was the miracle a Priest used.

It was activated by weaving holy words and offering prayers to the Gods.

It was also said that while the consumption of magic power was low, the power changed depending on the depth of one’s faith.

The attacks he fired contained a terrifying power. The stray bullets pierced the walls and floor, creating large holes. The attached mud sizzled, raising a stale smell and black smoke, melting everything it touched. It undoubtedly contained fatal power.

The strength of Clair’s prayer repelled every one of his deadly projectiles.

It could be said to be the fruit of her deep faith and the strong trust she placed in us, her comrades. However, if her consciousness or magic power were to be cut off, the miracle of the Barrier would immediately lose its effect.

“…I’m fine, Senpai! This much is okay…!”

She smiled gallantly, but the hand gripping her staff was trembling.

She was just being brave. It wouldn’t last much longer.

Marī was timing her attacks, firing magic arrows.

Bernkatze was defending against her attacks from his blind spots by turning the sludge that covered him into a wall. Every time he did so, the volume of darkness clinging to him was greatly reduced, but for some reason, it would well up to its original size or more after a while.

Alex also managed to land a strike with Marī’s support.

However, it wasn’t leading to a decisive blow. The inexhaustible black haze seemed to be constantly replenishing his strength and defense.

“He’s getting energy from somewhere… No way!”

I looked at the short sword he had plunged into the crystal.

Thump. Thump.

As if it were sucking something up.

The sludge wrapped around the short sword was pulsating.

I was right. That was the source of his power.

“I’ll take care of that.”

The battle was in a stalemate.

I had to have Marī continue to support Alex.

I hardened my resolve and aimed my crossbow. But I was concerned about the filthy sludge sticking to the short sword. Its horrifying, powerful pulsations made it seem like something that couldn’t be dealt with by a mere physical impact. It was a long shot. Was my only option to just fire the arrow?

At that moment, a flash of inspiration hit me.

I rummaged through my bag for the tool I had prepared. Found it.

I quickly tied a small bottle of Holy Water to the tip of an arrow.

I knew that the black mud contained a curse from our previous attempt at the dungeon.

I had prepared this in case we were hit by that attack again.

It was obvious that the mud was imbued with a curse.

If I washed it away with Holy Water, its power would surely be weakened.

“Hit!”

The modified bolt hit the cursed short sword.

The Holy Water scattered with force from the shattered bottle. The mud clinging to the short sword and crystal evaporated with a low groan as it came into contact with the Holy Water. The short sword quickly lost its power and fell out of the crystal—clattering to the floor with an empty sound.

“W-what!? Ahhh, my short sword!? D-d-did you figure out my unbeatable strategy!? …How!?”

Bernkatze had clearly started to panic.

His voice was dazed, but when he found me, he screamed furiously.

“Y-you, you did it? Did you… do it? …Kuh, damn it! Y-you with the mob face! You, of all people, you don’t have the right to get in my way!”

He completely forgot about Alex and charged at me.

However, his charge was easily blocked by an invisible wall.

Bernkatze, covered in a curse, was the personification of evil.

The miracles that Clair and the other Priests used didn’t allow anything evil to pass through.

There was no way he could get past the wall.

“D-damn it! What’s this measly wall!? I have a cheat skill! I’m the strongest in the world! I’ll force my way through! I’ll rape all of you at once!!”

“You won’t! You won’t be able to touch a single one of us!”

Clair, with a strong will, pushed him back.

She stood her ground with a dignified attitude, even as her trembling hands clung to her staff.

“I, and Marī… we love Senpai!!”

“Whaaaaaaaat!?”

Bernkatze’s eyes darted around.

He looked at our Party, appraising us.

And then, he made a face as if he couldn’t understand.

“Even Cindy, and Alex, everyone loves Senpai!! We’ve loved him for a very, very long time!! So, I don’t want you, of all people, to defile our feelings!!”

Bernkatze’s body was pushed back with a creaking sound.

The Barrier, which had the power of evil-cleansing, was increasing its range and strength in response to the power of Clair’s feelings.

“Look out!”

I caught Clair as she was about to collapse from her knees.

Her body, gripping mine tightly, was unbelievably hot.

Just like Alex, her entire body’s magic power was soaring with her emotions.

A light to exorcise darkness.

A radiance that could only be called that was being emitted from her body.

“Please, just don’t get in our way!!”

“Oooooooh!?”

A particularly strong light was released, as if in response to her scream.

The dark cloth that had been wrapped around Bernkatze was all stripped away.

“I-impossible… How could this happen… I was… invincible…”

Bernkatze, who was slammed against the wall by the force, had his eyes wide open. His eyes were still murky black, but they were no longer unfocused and eerie. The effect of the circlet’s control on his forehead must have been weakening.

“G-give it to me… your… body… to me…”

Obsession. It was a terrifying obsession.

Bernkatze was crawling with his ruined body.

He was looking straight at me.

“I-I’m the protagonist… Everything… belongs to me… Everything… should have gone well…”

The haze on his fingertips disappeared.

“Why… this is… not what was promised…”

It was a voice of supplication, of pleading.

“I want to go back… to my original world… I want to go back…”

Leaving behind words filled with regret.

The being that had tried to take over Bernkatze finally stopped.

# **84 - What Sleeps In The Heart Of Stillness (4)**

“You don’t have to worry about being taken over by touching Bern’s body, but please be careful not to touch the circlet and the gem.”

Taking Alex’s advice into account, I immediately disarmed the neutralized Bernkatze. I couldn’t find any signs of the Mara curse or any particular injuries on his body. His black hair had changed to gold, which must have been his original color. I securely bound his limbs with rope just in case.

“Cintāmaṇi accessory, huh?”

It was a name I was hearing for the first time, and I wondered what it meant.

That guy had called it a Cheat Item.

Infinite Continues.

In other words, he could revive if he died in this world.

It was exactly the kind of convenient item that would be prized as an Isekai Cheat Ability.

Alex said it was a Magic Tool that could transfer a personality to another body.

I was surprised by the obsession to live, even if it meant taking over another person’s body.

The skill that allowed him to absorb magic power from the short sword he stabbed was also a skill specialized in taking. Perhaps the Cheat Skill he boasted about included many other abilities to steal something from a target.

The existence of another Reincarnator. I had imagined it, but I never expected this kind of encounter. It wasn’t something I could talk to anyone about… It would likely take me some time to figure out how to process it.

“Even so, what was that guy…”

A mysterious entity that suddenly appeared and exposed its hostility.

Furthermore, he had harbored intense hatred toward the crystal in this room.

The crystal, which had been pierced by the short sword, was now half blackened and carbonized, whether from being polluted by the curse or from having its magic power stolen.

The Reincarnator clearly targeted this crystal with some intent. I didn’t know the reason. The quickest way would be to ask him directly, but from his behavior just now, he didn’t seem like the type I could hold a conversation with.

“Maybe his mind was worn out.”

I thought his behavior was unusual.

The words “I want to go back to my original world” he squeezed out at the end.

That might have been his true feelings.

A Cheat Ability that allowed him to revive no matter how many times he died.

Could the human spirit endure that?

Perhaps his heart had already been broken long ago.

Perhaps he had become a monster that attacked humans indiscriminately.

If he was completely stained by the idea that he could sacrifice any number of others to gain power, he wouldn’t be human anymore—while vaguely thinking about this, I picked up the short sword that had fallen beneath the crystal.

Glitter, the gem embedded in the pommel of the short sword shone ominously.

It was the Cintāmaṇi gem.

“!”

Damn it! By the time I realized it, everything was too late.

“—Got you, you idiot!”

My vision rapidly distorted.

“Heheheh! You should always prepare multiple trump cards, right!?”

Mocking laughter echoed.

Damn it! I was careless!

The world was swallowed by darkness.

I couldn’t see anything, I couldn’t hear anything.

It felt like standing in pitch-black darkness.

No, could I even say I was standing?

The ceiling, the floor—there was nothing here.

A sensation of floating alone in the void.

“You deserve it! I’m taking this body!”

“I won’t let you!”

“Hahaha! You talk a good game, but you can’t do anything!”

It seemed this was a Mental World, and we could hear each other’s voices.

“It’s no wonder you fell for it. This trump card has never been exposed before… You wouldn’t think a personality could be copied, would you?”

He started to explain with a voice of triumph.

“A copy of your personality? You’re not the real one!”

“…I forgot which one is the real one. I’ve saved my personality dozens, hundreds of times in the gem, and started over by taking over other people’s bodies every time I died… It’s pointless to even think about whether I’m the original.”

A dispassionate monologue.

I was surprised that he answered my question so honestly.

“You’re a Reincarnator, right?”

“Huh? How did you know that… Ah, are you a colleague, then? What, you should have told me that first! I would have killed you first!”

Pure killing intent pierced my exposed heart.

“A Reincarnator! Damn it, this is the worst! I remembered! It was a Reincarnator who killed the first me! Damn it! Damn it! Damnnnnnn it!”

“A Reincarnator… fighting a Reincarnator…”

Reincarnators were hostile to each other.

That revelation was shocking.

“I was given a Cheat Ability and reincarnated in another world! I should be able to live as I please! Eat delicious food, have women waiting on me, and kill anyone I don’t like! …But those smug Self-Governing Freaks showed up and crushed my country!!”

His intense emotions were reflected in the pitch-black world.

The figure of a man indulging in Drinking and Debauchery. He was covered in violence and sex.

A woman and her comrades appeared before him and beat him down unilaterally.

“This is the battle between Reincarnators…”

The man’s fighting was fierce, and the woman who crushed him unilaterally was terrifying.

An exchange of countless skills and magic. Both looked like demons to me.

“…That’s right, I’ll have my revenge on them! I’ll form a faction just like they did and crush the country they built—Marra!”

“Did you destroy Marra 100 years ago!?”

A Reincarnator built the Magic City Marra.

And Reincarnators were fighting each other.

I involuntarily raised my voice at the shocking new reality.

“100 years ago? Marra was destroyed?”

A dazed voice.

“I-I-It’s a lie… Marra was destroyed? 100 years ago? Then where have I been and what have I been doing for 100 years… Agh, gah.”

“H-hey! What’s wrong!?”

“If Marra was destroyed, why am I here!? Hey! This isn’t what was promised!”

“What promise!?”

He was clearly distraught.

Pish-pish… cracks appeared in the space.

They resonated with his tragic scream.

“Hey, who did you make a promise with and what was it!? Tell me!?”

“…Hahaha, hahahahaha. Hahahahahahahahaha!”

He was completely broken.

The cracked Mental World shattered with a rumbling sound.

The laughter eventually vanished, and the world returned to its original darkness.

“…At least give me back my body.”

Left behind, I was at a loss.

“Help! Someone, help me!”

“Be quiet.”

“Woah!?”

I never expected a reply to the words I muttered on a whim.

I fearfully turned around—or rather, wandered my senses around to do so.

Then, the outline of a person vaguely emerged from the darkness.

A pair of swirling horns extending from the sides of her head. Ears pointed like sharp blades.

Her long, flowing hair was as black as if the night had melted into it. Her downcast eyes, with long, sharp eyelashes, were dignified yet beautiful. I felt a calculated beauty from her, as if she were an artificial creation. Her outward features looked somewhat like a Demon, but she was enveloped in a mystical aura like a primitive Goddess rooted in regional faith.

Her dark green One-Piece Dress, like a black forest, spread out at the hem, making her look like a bride dressed in a Wedding Dress. However, a bold slit that opened wide from her chest to her navel tore at the image of demureness.

My gaze was naturally drawn into the deep valley between the two Holy Peaks visible from the slit.

“…Hey, how long are you going to stare at my chest… you idiot!”

A lightning bolt struck out of nowhere. A shocking pain ran through my entire body.

The pain was so intense I felt like I was going to die, but my consciousness was strangely clear.

The mysterious beautiful woman relentlessly stomped on my head, which had collapsed from the lightning strike.

“Bow your head before me. Kneel. Revere me with all your heart and soul!”

“Ow! Hey, Time-out!”

“Time out!? Not satisfied with the honor of an audience, you want to keep feeling my foot… Hehehe, what a pervert you are! ♥ But being faithful to your desires is not unpleasant! ♥ Come, come, I’ll stomp harder! ♥”

The mysterious beautiful woman ground the sole of her foot into my back with her toes.

She skillfully pinched and twisted my skin with her toes.

“Ow, ow, ow!? You know perfectly well that’s not what I meant!? I’m not a Masochist!”

“Hmm? I don’t understand what you mean, my dear. ♥”

“Gyaaa!”

She had no mystical quality. It was my illusion.

She was just an inherently mean bully with a bad attitude.

“Hah hah hah hah!”

I had no idea what was so amusing, but she laughed loudly, stomping all over my body. Since I couldn’t move a single finger, I had no choice but to endure it until she was satisfied.

“Hmm, this body is quite well-trained. It feels good to stomp on… Well, let me sample this area as well.”

“Eh?”

Ignoring my confusion, she skillfully flipped my body onto my back with just her foot.

Golden eyes. Elongated pupils—alien eyes reminiscent of a goat, horse, or herbivore—looked down at me. A red crescent moon floated at the corner of her mouth. A sadistic smile. Her gaze was fixed on my crotch.

“S-stop!”

“Don’t tell me you don’t like it; you know you do, don’t you? I know, my dear. ♥”

“I don’t know! I absolutely don’t know!!”

For some reason, her ears twitched happily at my desperate plea.

“But this place is quite bleak… Well, let me provide some staging!”

She snapped her fingers, and the world changed completely.

I was swept away by a flood of fabric that surged out of nowhere. When I came to, I was lying naked on a king-sized bed with a luxurious canopy. My position relative to her hadn’t changed.

Looking down at me, she showed a flash of her red tongue with an ecstatic expression.

She looked exactly like a snake preying on its victim.

“Hehehe, this is more like it. ♥”

She thrust the tip of her foot in front of my eyes, as if to show it off.

She pressed it against me and forced me to kiss her foot.

A sensation of something tingling and running throughout my entire body.

I was perplexed by the sudden rush of joy from an unknown source.

Worship and reverence for her flowed out of me from nowhere.

“Mmhmm. Your passionate gaze is not unpleasant. ♥”

She smiled, looking extremely satisfied with my reaction.

Her toe left my lips. I was surprised by the part of me that felt a sense of loss.

She then moved her foot, tracing a thin line toward the center of my body.

My heart, stomach, and then my crotch. The parts she caressed grew hot.

The weight of her foot slowly leaned onto my delicate zone.

“Ah, ah!”

Despite the strong pressure, excitement overcame the pain. My steel-hard extension pushed back against her foot. In response, she applied more force. The cycle repeated.

“Aren’t you happy? I can tell without you saying anything. Your spear is standing proudly as if it’s about to pierce the heavens. ♥”

She unilaterally ground and trampled the man. The rough action couldn’t be called an act of mutual affection between a man and a woman. Yet, perhaps because my own self, rubbed strongly by her soft sole, was as hot and hard as steel, I found the intense stimulation she gave me to be pleasant.

“The heat burning your body is transmitted to me as well. An uncontrollable pulsation… Hehehe, is your limit near now?”

The beautiful woman was aroused by my tormented appearance.

Her golden eyes shone brightly.

“Now, end your life miserably beneath my foot! ♥”

As those words reached my ears, I came.

The hot surge that spilled out of me. She was happily stirring the thick, sticky desire with the tip of her foot. A squelching sticky sound echoed. It felt strange to hear that sound coming from my crotch.

It was also my first time being sexually tormented.

A strange feeling, as if conflicting emotions of excitement and disgust, humiliation and affection, were wrestling inside my chest.

A period of clarity after ejaculation, the Sage Time.

I suddenly noticed that the beautiful woman stomping on me looked familiar.

She looked exactly like the silhouette I had seen inside the crystal.

“You’re the person in the Chalk Globe crystal… Could that crystal in the great hall also have been a Cintāmaṇi gem?”

The glow of that crystal was similar to the Cintāmaṇi gem.

I thought they might be the same thing, just a different size.

“Kuh, kufufu! Ah-hah-hah-hah! Sage Time! I see! That’s a good phrase! Kufufu, what a clever wordplay… I thought you were just a dull man, but you have a surprisingly sharp side!”

She covered her mouth with the back of her right hand and narrowed her eyes as she laughed. I didn’t know what was so funny, but it seemed to have struck a chord, as she was shaking her shoulders and holding her stomach with her left hand. Her breasts, supported by her left hand from below, were further emphasized, bouncing significantly as she laughed. Looking up at her from below, I felt heat return to my core.

Naturally, she sensed my reaction through the sole of her foot.

Her passionate, melting golden eyes crawled over my entire body.

“Before I answer that question… I think I’ll enjoy you a little more. ♥”

As she declared that, a thick sensuality wafted from her entire body.

In the face of the potent and dangerous pheromones that would arouse anyone regardless of gender, the reason that had returned during the Sage Time was effortlessly defeated. It evaporated.

“Come now, love me with all your heart and soul! ♥”

Her dress dissolved and vanished like the wind. My consciousness was fixed on the overflowing, voluptuous body. Dripping drool from both her upper and lower mouth, she looked nothing more than a ferocious predator.

# **85 - What Sleeps In The Heart Of Stillness (5)**

The woman, with a lithe, leopard-like physique, went on all fours and scooped up the white fluid I had squeezed out with her fingers, bringing it to her mouth. She licked each finger deliberately as if savoring the taste slowly. Humming softly in her throat, she let out a sigh.

“Ah, the rich taste of life, savored after so long, how utterly exquisite… a true nectar. My very core aches and strongly demands your essence.♥”

She crawled up from my feet and straddled my abdomen, sitting down heavily on me.

# **95 - Visiting The Guild**

The Carriage Guild had a splendid building, befitting a place with thriving trade.

“Unfortunately, we are not running a regular service this time of year,”

“That’s a problem.”

“Furthermore, snow has already begun to accumulate in the northern frontier. Few people would dare to send a carriage out at this time of year. For the Guild, it’s not profitable to run a regular service as there are many dangers and fewer customers.”

“Do you have any ideas?”

“In that case, why don’t you inquire at the Adventurer’s Guild?”

“Yes. While the Carriage Guild doesn’t run a regular service, merchant associations and traveling merchants prepare their own carriages to transport people and goods. Her yellow eyes sparkled with the success of her prank.

She was no longer the Goddess of the Night but more like a whimsical devil.

Unable to withstand the atmosphere, I took the waiter girl’s hand, discreetly pressed a tip into it, and decided to quickly leave the restaurant.

I walked around the town with Ratori again.

Since my stomach was full, I figured I could resist the tempting aromas from the food stalls for a while.

It was not good to be too extravagant since the journey had just begun.

I needed to buy the necessary items for our departure the day after tomorrow.

I planned to stock up mainly on preserved foods.

Originally, I hadn’t been given much in the way of preserved foods, and the ingredients we brought from George’s village were mostly used up on the journey so far.

This was according to plan, as I had intended to make full preparations for the journey in this town.

What I hadn’t expected was that the town of Kōgushi was many times more magnificent and prosperous than I had imagined. It overflowed with people, goods, and vitality.

While the Slums in Libra were much larger in terms of the town’s scale, the public order and atmosphere of this town were overwhelmingly superior.

I remember some adventurers I knew who had made a name for themselves in Libra and then moved their base to the town of Kōgushi. I felt I now understood the reason for that.

As I pondered this while browsing, I noticed something.

The prices of food items across the board had risen compared to yesterday.

Intrigued by this, I spoke to the owner of a cart loaded with fruits and vegetables.

“Those apples look delicious.”

“Oh, young man. I’m confident in the taste! Are you buying some?”

“Hmm. But on second thought, the apples sold yesterday seemed bigger, didn’t they? And the price was cheaper.”

“If you’re going to find fault, just go home already.”

“No, no, you’re confident in the taste, right? I’ll buy them at this price.”

“Heheh, is that so! My apologies then!”

I took a bite of the apple I bought right there.

Apples in this world were mostly sour, but his apples had a definite sweetness. As expected from someone confident in the taste, they weren’t bad.

“Yes. It’s delicious.”

“I’m happy to hear that.”

“By the way, it looks like the prices at other shops have also risen across the board compared to yesterday. Do you know anything about that?”

The apple seller made a grim face at my question, but after looking left and right, he secretly beckoned me closer.

Approaching cautiously, he whispered in my ear.

“Actually, there’s a rumor circulating among the merchants. That’s why we all agreed to raise the prices just a little.”

He referred to it as a rumor, but it was likely highly accurate information.

In other words, it was information they didn’t want to speak about openly.

“Judging by your appearance, you’re an adventurer, aren’t you? If you want to know more details, you should go to the Guild. It should lead to some job opportunities.”

“Thank you. I’ll take another apple as a bonus.”

Saying that, I added some extra money to the price as a tip for the information.

“Thanks!”

I left the spot with the apple seller’s words at my back.

Ratori, walking beside me, tangled her arm in mine, drawing her body closer under the pretense of avoiding the crowd.

“What’s wrong?”

“Something caught my attention, so I’m thinking of stopping by the Adventurer’s Guild.”

“Should I go back to the inn first?”

“I think it’s okay for you to come with me. It’s better to have you by my side in case something happens.”

“Okay.”

I answered with confidence, trying to cheer up her body, which had slightly tensed up.

A bad rumor that affected the town’s prices.

I had a slight idea of what it was.

We arrived at the Adventurer’s Guild.

I immediately headed to the reception desk where I knew the official.

He seemed to have recognized me right away.

He welcomed me with an uncharacteristic forced smile.

“What brings you here today?”

“I heard a rumor.”

“I see.”

He seemed to understand with just that, stroking his chin and nodding.

“Let’s not talk here. Let’s discuss it in the back.”

Saying that, he invited us into a private room behind the counter.

As soon as he sat on the sofa, he cut straight to the point.

“It seems a war has started in the west.”

I nodded quietly at his words, prompting him to continue.

“You must have heard the talk about the Marra Dungeon being conquered, right? Apparently, the son of the Marquis of Libra was in the conquering Party, and the Marquis of Libra allowed his son to govern a piece of land as a reward for that achievement. The land that was left empty after the disaster became a buffer zone with the surrounding countries, but… this recent chain of events has reignited the dispute over land ownership. A merchant happened to witness a skirmish between the armies on the western border, and since he was heading for this town, the information got here.”

As expected, Alex was involved.

I had heard directly from him that he would return from being an adventurer to a noble and would be tasked with leading the Marquis of Libra’s army to protect the former Marra territory.

“My father is still a noble of Marra, even though the country is ruined.”

Why was such a large-scale army necessary for the dungeon conquest?

At first, I had mistakenly thought it was to prevent the discovered treasures from being looted, but the truth was more complex.

His father, Iskandar, the Marquis of Libra, apparently had roots in the Tranchère family, a noble family of Marra that was destroyed over 100 years ago.

Therefore, he had shown a very strong stance regarding the ownership of the ruins of Marra.

At the same time, he was also keen on collecting the magical artifacts, the heritage of Marra.

The dungeon’s conquest was one of his long-cherished desires.

It must have been an unexpected joy that his son, Alex, and his Party happened to challenge the dungeon, successfully conquered the hidden area, and discovered the numerous legacies sleeping there.

More importantly, that dungeon was still active.

The excellent magical technology of the time, which had brought fame to the continent, still existed.

The Marquis thought that since the dungeon itself could not be brought back, leaving it as it was would mean letting “the most significant heritage” slip through his fingers to others.

As a result, he took the aggressive step of annexing the entire former Marra region into the Libra territory.

Marquis Iskandar made that decision, prepared to swallow all the friction with the surroundings and the dissatisfaction of the people living in the Libra territory that would arise from it.

Now, the impact of that decision was starting to manifest in the world.

“You don’t seem very surprised. Oh, right, you’re from Libra, aren’t you? So you must have had a few chances to hear about it.”

“Yes. I’m an adventurer, as you can see.”

“Gahaha! That’s certainly true, that’s hilarious! Gahahahahaha!”

He took my words as a joke and laughed with such force that it seemed his face might break.

“Gahaha! So, how much of that rumor did you hear in town?”

He asked in a friendly tone, but his eyes weren’t laughing.

He was interrogating me about who I heard it from and what exactly I heard.

“Nothing specific. Just that there was a rumor. The food prices in the market all rose uniformly compared to yesterday. It’s only natural to suspect that something might have happened.”

“…Hmm, I see. Well, I suppose that can’t be helped then.”

He closed his eyes, seeming satisfied with my answer.

It seemed he wouldn’t press the matter further.

“So, what are you going to do? You’re not going to abandon the quest and run off to some other town, are you?”

“I will fulfill the quest I accepted properly. Unless the quest is canceled, of course.”

“That’s a relief. You’re reliable.”

He relaxed his cheeks, looking slightly relieved.

It seemed that was his biggest concern.

If a Silver Rank adventurer suddenly canceled, the Guild’s reputation would be completely ruined, especially since he intended to put the client in his debt.

He wanted to avoid that at all costs.

“This is the time of the annual festival. It’s the town’s biggest earning season. The whole town is enveloped in a bright and lively atmosphere. No one wants to hear a rumor that could incite anxiety. You understand, don’t you?”

I nodded at his words.

“At least until the new year begins, until the festival ends, we don’t want to be swayed by mere rumors. The various Guilds will cooperate to deal with malicious ones… In other words, what you heard here is for your ears only.”

“Yes, of course.”

Ratori also nodded quietly.

“Thank you for the valuable information.”

I bowed deeply in gratitude and quickly left the room.

Outside the Guild, the sky had become overcast in the short time we were inside.

I wondered if Alex, who was likely at the center of the turmoil, was safe.

I gazed at the cloudy sky and, for a moment, thought about my comrades in Libra.

+++

# **99 - A Letter To Libra**

The wheels turned, marking time.

The bustling line of carriages, constantly shifting at the distant terminal, had a busyness that was somewhat reminiscent of my previous life.

I ran my pen across the paper while glancing at that scene from the window.

I had come to the Carriage Guild with Ratori again.

I was writing a letter using the stationery and paper I had bought at the market.

It was addressed to the comrades and friends I had left behind in Libra.

I didn’t know what would happen with the skirmish on the border.

Still, driven by anxiety, I felt I had to do something.

But once I tried to write, I found it difficult.

It had only been one week since I left the town.

The period when I had been estranged from them was much longer.

And yet, when I tried to put my feelings into words, apologies, repentance, and gratitude for them kept welling up endlessly.

If I wrote as my emotions dictated, the sentences would become completely unmanageable.

I racked my brain and thought about it, but in the end, I decided to keep it to a simple status update.

I had left town due to a sudden quest, but I was doing well.

I was grateful that I had met them.

I wanted to see them all again someday. We would definitely meet.

It was something along those lines.

I proofread the completed draft to check for any flaws.

“You’re quite skilled, aren’t you? You write such beautiful letters.”

“It’s like a skill you acquired in your youth. When I was a kid, before I became an adventurer, I used to earn my daily bread by being a scribe and reader.”

Ratori, who had been watching my work from the side, exclaimed in admiration.

Once the draft was complete, the rest was simple work.

I became a human copy machine, prepared several copies with the same wording, wrote the destination and names on the front, folded the paper like origami, and sealed it with sealing wax. The letter was complete.

“There’s a way to seal it like that, too, isn’t there?”

“It’s not an important document. I just wanted to save money on an envelope.”

The letter culture in this world was quite haphazard, as the format wasn’t fixed.

There were various types, like parchment scrolls, documents rolled up and stuffed into wooden cylinders, or even written directly on wooden boards. It was no exaggeration to call it freestyle.

The paper I happened to get was thin, so I did it this way, but if it had been a thick and hard-to-fold type, I think I would have gone through the extra effort of tying it with a string or sending it in a wooden cylinder.

“I’d like to send this.”

I paid the shipping fee presented by the surly official and entrusted the letter to him.

All I could do was pray that it would arrive safely.

---

The Slums that spread outside the city walls of Libra were continuously expanding.

It had expanded over many years and was becoming established as a downtown area.

There were citizens within the walls who found this annoying, but they were not so foolish as to stir up a fuss needlessly. On the contrary, they even thought it was fine as it was if it functioned as “another wall” to keep the refugees from pouring into the city.

In the Slums, which were outwardly calm but inwardly chaotic, it was not uncommon for people to suddenly disappear.

Even a skilled adventurer was no exception.

They might have gotten caught up in an incident on a street corner or had an accident during a quest.

I could think of countless reasons.

There were many who envied those who had achieved success.

The man who had been the center of attention suddenly stopped showing up at the Guild.

Something must have happened to him.

The rumor, with added embellishments, quickly swam around among the adventurers, serving as good gossip to talk about over drinks.

“Tsk, what an idiot! He gets cocky and dies right away!”

“He just wasn’t skilled enough after all.”

“And to think he could have gotten some leftovers from his old comrades. What a waste.”

Dead men tell no tales.

They gossiped about him while they had the chance.

“Did he really die? I heard he was a scumbag who would survive even if it meant sacrificing his comrades, didn’t I?”

“I agree. If anything, he was said to be a man who was obsessed with money, so wouldn’t it be more likely to be a financial problem?”

“You mean he ran away, chased by debt? Now that you mention it, there was a big manhunt one night a while ago.”

“I think that one was about a woman. A southern one. Hey, the request was posted on the bulletin board for a while, too, wasn’t it?”

The story of a dead person, especially an adventurer, usually didn’t last long.

That’s because it was part of their daily lives. The fact that the topic lingered, contrary to the usual, was proof that he was a special person to them.

For adventurers who gambled with their lives, a Level 1 adventurer who had survived for five years was something alien to them and a person who left a deep impression.

The endless, unanswered questions continued to be repeated.

The boneless, fleshless fish drifted like a ghost.

“I don’t like it.”

A gruff-voiced adventurer, showing off his armor of trained muscles, growled lowly.

He gulped down the overflowing mug of ale in one go.

Still, he didn’t feel any better. He wasn’t even getting drunk.

“All of them, they’re always talking about him.”

Danio didn’t like it.

That weak and feeble man, for whatever reason, was promoted to Silver Rank before he was. He didn’t like that one bit. He felt like his guts were boiling. He even felt like strangling him in a fit of rage.

And yet, even after he was gone, he was still dominating the conversation.

Every time, that man’s face flashed in Danio’s mind.

He didn’t like it. He didn’t like it. There was no way he couldn’t like it.

“Tch!”

He crushed the mug in his hand out of frustration.

The ring of the clasp bounced like a spring and landed on the table of the group that was talking excitedly about that man.

Danio silenced the ones who were about to protest with a single glare.

Not only his stern appearance but also his skill as an adventurer easily overwhelmed them.

Danio snorted roughly, seeing them fall silent like frogs stared at by a snake.

“Hah! You gutless pieces of shit! Go do a quest or something before you start talking! You worthless scumbags who just drink all day and whine, don’t you dare pretend to be proper adventurers, you bald morons!”

It was a sermon from a bald man who drank all day and whined without doing any quests.

They didn’t have the skill to retort, “You’re the one talking.”

Their faces were bright red, but they meekly got up and fled outside the Guild.

“Don’t shit your pants so easily.”

He still didn’t like their attitude.

He thought that guy would have glared back at him and argued, even though he knew he couldn’t win a fistfight.

Thinking that only irritated Danio even more.

He was just as swayed by the man who had disappeared as the other adventurers.

“Where in the world are you wandering around, you sterile bastard?”

Danio ordered more ale to distract himself from his terrible mood.

He was still not drunk enough.

Some time after that event, a single person visited the Adventurer’s Guild.

A petite girl with a graceful air about her. She was a full-fledged adventurer.

She was wrapped in bandages to hide the cursed marks she had received on an adventure.

She looked pitiful, but if her limbs were intact, it was considered a minor injury for an adventurer.

If anything, she was attracting curious glances.

That was because she was one of the Party members of the rumored man.

“Quest. Finished.”

She didn’t seem to care about the gazes that clung to her.

She went straight to the Guild counter and stated her business matter-of-factly.

The official picked up the item that had been handed to him and checked it.

“Yes. No problems. Then, please wait a moment while I prepare your reward.”

“Mm.”

After a while, the official returned.

Something other than the leather pouch with the reward was offered to her.

“This, what is it?”

“It’s a letter delivered to the Guild. It’s addressed to you.”

She had no one who would send her a letter.

She had no idea who it could be. She furrowed her brows and tilted her head.

She scrutinized the letter, which was sealed with wax.

“If you can’t read, I can read it for you.”

“No thanks.”

It wasn’t uncommon for people to be unable to read or write.

She was especially seen as such because of her halting way of speaking.

In fact, she wasn’t good at reading and writing.

Even so, she knew what a letter was from her knowledge.

She also understood the meaning of it being sealed with wax.

It would be better to avoid opening it here, where there were many eyes and ears.

She naturally came to that conclusion. She carefully put it away in her pocket.

Having finished her business at the Guild, she weaved her way through the crowd.

She turned into several alleys and hurried along the intricate narrow paths.

It was what you would call an animal trail, not a place for people to walk.

“…Damn it, where did she go!?”

“We lost her again! That arrogant brat!”

The girl, wrapped in bandages to hide her curse marks, looked incredibly weak to the casual observer.

Even taking into account that she was an active adventurer, she looked like an attractive prey to the thugs.

However, as a Silver Rank adventurer and a scout who was always working to spot monsters and traps for the safety of her Party, there was no way she wouldn’t notice the malice of people with impure thoughts.

“Bye bye.”

The thugs cursed as they lost their prey.

She whispered, seeing them from the gap in the alley.

For her, this exchange was a mundane part of her daily life.

After making sure she had completely shaken off her pursuers, she headed for her real destination.

She had a house in a part of the Slums close to the city of Libra, where public order was more stable.

Originally, this area had been developed for the city’s expansion, but it was never incorporated into the city due to the large number of refugees who had poured in before the wall was erected.

Because of this, many residents in this area had a stable livelihood.

It was considered the wealthy area within the Slums of Libra.

“Yoo-hoo, it’s Cindy.”

“…Why are you here?”

The homeowner was surprised by the sudden visitor.

The dark circles under her eyes were clearly visible.

Her messy hair and crumpled clothes significantly detracted from her beauty.

The female mage was rumored to be a beauty at the Guild.

This was her secret appearance that she would not want anyone to know about.

It could be said to be proof of the deep trust between the two of them, but at this particular moment, it was mostly due to the fact that her judgment had been impaired by her consecutive all-nighters.

Marī looked down at Cindy with a suspicious look.

“I don’t think I ever invited you into my house.”

“I followed Zaryū. Then I found it.”

“Unbelievable. Why are you doing something like that?”

“Hobby.”

Marī couldn’t find the words to respond to Cindy, who said that with an air of confidence.

Since standing and talking was awkward, Marī invited her into the house.

The room was cluttered in a mess.

It was in a state where there was barely enough space to step.

Cindy didn’t seem to mind it at all and quickly sat down on a chair.

“What’s so fun about following a man like that?”

“Marī does it too.”

“Huh?”

“You always followed him with your eyes.”

“I don’t think so…”

Marī immediately denied it, but her voice gradually became weaker.

She almost let her consciousness be led to reflect on the past by Cindy’s words, but she let go of it at the last moment.

She shook her head, clearing the haze from her thoughts.

“So, what do you need from me?”

“Read letter.”

“Letter?”

Marī quietly accepted the letter that was offered to her.

“It’s still sealed with wax. I don’t feel any magical presence either. It looks like just a plain letter?”

Marī couldn’t guess the reason why Cindy would come to her specifically for this.

Her answer was simple.

“This, came from Zaryū.”

Marī gasped at Cindy’s words.

Upon closer inspection of the address, it did indeed look similar to his handwriting.

What could possibly be written in the letter?

Why was it delivered to Cindy and not to her?

Why didn’t he say a single word to her before leaving town?

Marī suppressed her eagerness, closed her eyes, and took her time to sort out her thoughts and emotions.

She chased the noisy distractions out of her mind and cleared her consciousness.

She slowly exhaled and opened her eyelids.

Her gaze was as sharp as if she were wearing a mask of ice.

She had switched to Adventurer mode.

So that she could calmly accept whatever was written in it.

“I’m opening it.”

+++

# **100 - In The Snow Mountains (vs. Troll)**

It was noon on the second day after leaving the town of Kōgushi.

We were under attack by monsters.

While we were slowly advancing, packing down the snow on the severely snow-covered mountain road, a horde of monsters suddenly attacked with fierce roars.

However, everyone here was a veteran adventurer.

They immediately readied their weapons, even as they cried out in surprise and caution at the ambush.

Having quickly established a defensive formation, they held back the monsters’ frontal charge.

There was a dull sound of bending iron.

Fierce clashes were happening everywhere.

I was positioned in the center of the formation.

Given my title as a Silver Rank, I was entrusted with the most crucial position, guarding the merchants and non-combatants. Although it was a safe position with other adventurers protecting the front and rear, I felt a surge of tension in a situation where I was completely stuck between sword clashes and angry shouts.

The wind swept through the mountain path with a “zaa” sound.

Snow swirled up, and I felt a sense of danger as my field of vision rapidly narrowed.

A white darkness was assailing us.

“Gyaah!”

A bright red splash erupted simultaneously with a scream.

A shriek mixed with the angry shouts flying about.

The monsters raised a battle cry.

“Don’t you dare leave your posts!”

The man acting as the leader frantically yelled.

Few voices responded.

Was it just that they had no margin for error, or had most of them already been defeated?

Something was approaching with a heavy, dull thud that could be felt even through the snowy ground.

A dark shadow abruptly burst into my white-tinged vision.

“It’s a bear!”

A club was swung down above the head of the man who shouted that, seeing the shadow.

In that instant, he was cut down to half his height.

“You idiot! This is a Troll!”

It had elephant-like skin, gray hide, and dark eyes sunken in its orbits.

Its physique, easily exceeding two meters, was covered in thick muscle and fat.

Its legs were short, but its long, extended arms became weapons just by being swung.

It was a giant body, easily mistaken for a bear, but it was a much more terrifying existence.

“Hey, you! You’re a Silver Rank, aren’t you! Do something about that monster!”

“I know!”

Before another victim was claimed, at least I had to hold it here.

I tightly grasped the sword in my hands with both, forcefully stepped in, dove under the Troll’s feet, and swung with all my might.

The tip of the sword smoothly cut the skin and severed the fat—but the blade could not pass beyond that.

“Amazing! You’re not bad!”

An excited heckle flew from behind me, but my heart was not calm.

I had intended to swing through with the image of cutting off one of its legs.

However, in reality, I didn’t even reach the bone.

“Alex should have been able to kill it with that hit just now.”

Even if I was benefiting from the Level Up, I probably had absolutely no skill in handling the weapon.

I was far from the revered figure I envisioned in my mind.

He had definitely defeated a Troll alone when he was Level 6.

Judging by simple Level, I should have more than double the difference compared to him back then.

Yet, this pathetic state. I could weep at my own incompetence.

But, the attack passed. It did pass.

Back then, I couldn’t pierce the Troll’s tough skin.

Now, I have a glimmer of hope.

“Uwoooohh!”

The improvement in physical ability from my Level was strongly drawn out by willpower.

I put my fighting spirit into every strike as I swung the sword.

I steadily chipped away at the Troll’s body, evading its attacks—the powerful, roaring strike of a massive arm that sent up snow, the club repeatedly swung down to make mince of me, the stomping, the kicking—all delivered from its massive frame.

My speed was completely superior.

“Tsk!!”

It discarded its club and tried to grab me with a strike using both hands.

I dodged it with a huge vertical leap, then used its joined fists as a foothold to aim for its neck. I plunged in, colliding with my entire body, aimed at the throat beneath the jaw, and thrust the blade in.

The tip of the blade bit into something hard with a loud crack.

It must have stabbed into the spine.

I released the sword, which was now completely stuck, and landed on the ground.

The blood flowing from the wound stained the entire area red.

The Troll sank to its knees with a heavy zun sound.

Surely, its strength must have run out.

A heavy, sideways impact struck my head as I thought that.

I plunged headfirst, sliding onto the snow.

“Gah, gehoh…”

This was no time to cower in pain.

“W-a second one!?”

The eyes I quickly raised caught a Troll that was the spitting image of the one I had just defeated.

I didn’t know if they were brothers or family, but I couldn’t believe there was one more.

Its bloodshot eyes glared at me.

It was clear that it directed anger and hatred towards me.

If it intended to avenge its comrade, I would accept the challenge.

As I glared back with that intent, the creature laughed.

Why?

As I wondered, it picked up the club dropped by the fallen Troll. That’s bad. An ominous sixth sense shot up my spine. The creature, having readied the club, aimed not at me but at the carriage.

“You won’t!”

I kicked the ground with all my strength.

At the end of the swing of the club, which the Troll wielded like a baseball bat, was the carriage carrying the merchants and Ratori. It intended to destroy what we were protecting first, in retaliation for its slain comrade.

I slid my body into the attack’s trajectory without hesitation.

The result would be determined in an instant. I couldn’t afford to hesitate.

I threw myself into the attack to protect Ratori.

I prepared for the impact with all my heart and soul.

“Ugh, fuhn-nuguguguguuuh!!”

In an instant, my consciousness flew.

I felt like I would be torn apart by the impact.

I twisted my head and neck, which felt like they were ripping off, back with sheer willpower.

All the equipment I was wearing couldn’t withstand the killing blow and burst off completely.

The bones and muscles in my whole body screamed, but that didn’t matter.

“Ugh, gigigi!!”

I grit my teeth, caught the club with both hands, and braced my legs.

The entirety of the shock rushed through my body. A few seconds, or dozens of seconds? Time was stretched out. Such a strange sensation. Something warm and thick trickled down my lip. Blood. My nose was bleeding. Blood also overflowed from the corner of my mouth.

A sense of exhaustion, as if my internal organs had completely fallen out.

My entire body was overcome by a chill so intense that the snow felt warm.

I clearly understood that I was on the brink of death.

But.

“Ha… haha, ha… How’s that, I stopped it…!”

I had completely received and prevented the Troll’s retaliatory strike.

The Troll’s face, which should have been flushed red with rage, had completely paled.

The club slipped from its hands and sank into the ground, which had turned into mud.

I picked up a sword from the corpse of a dead adventurer and walked towards the Troll.

The Troll retreated, inch by inch.

“Gugaaaaaah!”

“Uwooooooh!”

The Troll let out a fierce roar and swung its fist down.

I dodged it with a half-step and slashed its arm.

The counter, utilizing the Troll’s own brute strength, tore the skin, pierced the fat, cut through the muscle’s armor, and reached the bone, which was as hard as steel. I desperately gripped the hilt to avoid being swept away by the shock and not to drop the sword.

The sword gave out before I did.

The blade snapped in the middle and became unusable.

“Damn it! Again!”

An expletive involuntarily escaped my lips.

I protected my slashed arm, and with a thrust of the broken sword into the neck of the Troll, which was screaming in pain, I slammed my fist hard into the side of its face. The Troll, eyes rolling, collapsed, spitting foamy blood from its mouth, and convulsed repeatedly.

“Did I… get it?”

I watched it for a while, worried it might get up, but it seemed completely dead.

I somehow understood that what you could call the Troll’s presence was fading from the massive corpse lying on the ground.

“Hah, hah… hah.”

I sighed in relief, collapsed from my knees onto the spot, and sat with a thump.

I had somehow managed to win against the Troll, which was considered a major obstacle among adventurers.

However, in exchange, my body was a wreck, as you can see, and my weapon and armor were completely ruined.

I didn’t think I could push myself any further.

But, fortunately, the sounds of battle had completely stopped everywhere, and the adventurers’ battle cry reached me on the wind.

It seemed we had successfully repelled the monsters.

“I wanna take a bath.”

The desire that came out of my mouth in my relief was not the joy of victory, the exultation of survival, or the high of realizing my own growth and strength, but the utterly mundane desire to soothe the physical exhaustion—the kind that made you feel like your whole body had turned to lead—after getting thoroughly covered in blood and mud.

+++

# **101 - The Northern Town Of Daiden**

After that, we weren’t attacked by monsters, and with the good weather, we smoothly completed our journey and, as scheduled, arrived at our destination—the northern town of Daiden—on the evening of the fourth day after leaving Kōgushi.

This was a Dwarf town.

It was a town of white smoke, with steam from hot springs and smoke from blacksmiths billowed up.

It was also said to be a noisy town where the sound of mining from the mines echoed day and night.

Dwarves would be a classic fantasy race.

In my previous life, they were often described as “stumpy little people with barrel-like bodies, thick limbs, and magnificent beards,” and the Dwarves in this world looked exactly like that.

Their height was roughly between 120 and 150 centimeters.

That’s about the height of my waist to my chest. They were shorter than adult women. But their width was sometimes double mine, which was interesting. Since many of them grew long beards and hair, their rounded silhouettes were also strangely endearing.

Perhaps it was to match their physique, but I felt that the various buildings adorning the townscape also incorporated many rounded designs. The overpasses with gentle curves, the gates of the shopping district, and the park with a fountain in the shape of a dragon—which was spewing steam and hot spring water instead of normal water—had colorful circular tiles.

Both Ratori and I were wide-eyed at the exotic scenery of the Dwarf town.

I enjoyed sightseeing with her for a while.

The Dwarves were friendly, or rather, they had no reserve.

“Hey, you young man, you need a present for your pretty lady, don’t you! If you don’t show a little backbone, she’ll cheat on you right away!”

“That’s right! My goldwork is what I’d recommend!”

“No way! Mine’s way better! The gems are bigger, too!”

“What did you say!?”

“Wanna go!?”

They would bluntly push in, ignore me, and start boasting about their work.

They didn’t throw punches, but their mouths were on fire. Before I knew it, more and more craftsmen gathered, and they started arguing back and forth. Let them do as they please.

I ignored the boisterous Dwarf craftsmen and led Ratori away by the hand.

“Hehehe, I’m not planning to cheat, so don’t you worry, okay?”

“I appreciate that.”

“A lovely gift is always welcome, though, don’t you think, my darling husband? ♥”

“I don’t have enough money since I need to get new weapons and armor.”

“Weapons are more important than me?”

“I need the weapons because you’re important to me.”

“Heh, hehehe! I know that, so don’t pout, okay? ♥ Oh, look, look! Look at that! Don’t you think that’d look really good on me!?”

Ratori snuggled up to me and teased me like that.

She seemed to have been very worried about me because I was so beaten up after the Troll battle.

When I was resting in the carriage as one of the wounded, Ratori had been taking devoted care of me, so I figured this behavior was a kind of reaction to the stress she had been under.

I had earned an additional reward from the client, as I was highly praised for my single-handed defense of the carriage and for defeating two vicious Trolls alone. The heavy weight of the bag of gold coins lightened my mood a bit.

The Dwarf warrior, Bakuga.

He had taken great pains to help me back then when I was a beginner.

He had taught me various things that I still use today, such as tips for discerning good weapons and armor, how to tell if coins are genuine or counterfeit, and how to explore a cave.

It looked more like a bar from any angle.

A red-haired receptionist noticed me and spoke first.

“Yeah, that’s right.”

How did he drink his alcohol?

Rock-breaking. Another name for “Dwarf style.”

They put chilled metal instead of ice in their drinks.

In other words, it’s on the rocks.

I remember there being stainless steel cubes in my previous life.

The good thing about it is that it doesn’t melt like ice, so the alcohol doesn’t get diluted.

In this world, where low-alcohol drinks were the mainstream, only Dwarves would enjoy drinking fire liquor—distilled liquor—in that way.

“The drink tastes better when your tongue is dry.”

It felt like he was just spitting out whatever came to mind and stringing it together.

Contrary to his stern appearance, he was talkative.

He acted like an honest and taciturn man during adventures, but in town, especially when he was at a bar, words would flow out of him like spring water. That was the kind of man he was.

Many self-centered adventurers wanted to be the center of attention.

I was rather an unusual type because I was interested in what he had to say and listened intently, and now that I think about it, he might have liked that about me.

“Actually, I can hear the voices of stones.”

“The voices of stones?”

I asked back, not understanding the meaning of the words that had been so abruptly spoken.

“Mhm. The stones speak to me.”

“That’s amazing.”

I thought it was some kind of metaphor or an expression that was only understood by his own race.

I ate my food while it was still warm and gave a few casual acknowledgements.

Bakuga’s eyes stared at me.

Damn it, I thought. I had been too careless, and now I had put him in a bad mood.

But that was an unnecessary worry.

“There are three of them there.”

He pointed to the pouch on my waist and said that.

At first, I didn’t understand what he meant, but I quickly realized the meaning of his words.

I quickly searched inside my pouch.

Indeed, there were three palm-sized stones I had picked up for throwing.

“Gahahahahahahaha!”

Bakuga laughed with satisfaction when he saw the expression on my face, my eyes wide with surprise.

“Awesome! Can all Dwarves do this!?”

“The only one besides me who claimed to have this ability… was my great-grandfather.”

At the time, I hadn’t yet realized I had my own Divine Protection.

I had a strong admiration for the cheat-like abilities of reincarnated people, so I was strongly fascinated by Bakuga’s special ability.

“What did these stones say!?”

“Mhm. They said, ‘We are stones, hard stones’… They said that with pride.”

“That’s so cool!”

Thinking about it now, it wasn’t cool at all.

I was quite drunk at the time.

I also remembered that, thanks to the rock-breaking drink he had foisted on me, I had been tormented by a terrible hangover the next day.

But perhaps because my praise made him feel good, Bakuga broke into a satisfied smile.

“Actually, this is a secret… So, don’t tell anyone what you heard from me, okay?”

Feeling good, he said that to me and told me his secret.

I believed him and had come all the way to Daiden.

“—I see. There’s only one weirdo who would say something like that. Could you wait here for a moment? Listen up? I’ll be right back, so you absolutely, do not, move, from this spot!”

The receptionist said that and ran out of the guild in a rush.

She was in such a hurry; I was worried she might trip in the snow.

She had also been drinking, so would she be okay?

“Are you really going to wait?”

Ratori asked me in a low voice.

“Doesn’t that attitude worry you a little? I feel like something is strange.”

“It does worry me a little, but we don’t have any other leads.”

“I have a bad feeling about this.”

“Haha, that’s a problem…”

I was influenced by Ratori’s serious demeanor.

This was probably a warning or caution from her Divine Protection of Inspiration.

I wasn’t the type of person who would be happy to have trouble come my way.

I would prefer to get out of here as soon as possible.

“…But I don’t think there’s any point in running away now. She’s already got our information. It’s better to be bold.”

I said that and puffed out my chest. It was a bluff, and a good one at that.

I hadn’t yet procured a new weapon and armor to replace what I had lost in the Troll battle.

If things developed into a conflict, those conditions would work against me.

“It’s okay; I’ll figure it out.”

I wondered if I had chosen the wrong way to proceed with this quest.

I held that anxiety in my heart and quietly waited for the receptionist to return.
